The light that reflects off the clippers (which can be seen in my mirror&#x27;s reflection) can kind of make lines appear on my hair that aren&#x27;t really there. This mostly happens when cutting the hair on the back of my head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The blades cut really well. For questions of how close these cut, you have to understand that decent quality clippers have 2 screws affixing the to blade. If you loosen these guys, you can push the top blade back and tighten with less clearance for a zero cut. Be careful not to go to far, or you risk scalping yourself.You may also adjust the adjustment lever for more tension. Final A adjustments can be made for the throw of the cutting blades by turning large plastic side scree to decrease noise. Note: the Conned heir brand build many of thier models to not have blades adjusted, rendering them useless for short cuts. The motor designs are weaker, and the are beaucoup weak plastic pieces in the drive train lending themselves too much movement, inprecision and rapid blade wear. These budget minded wahlshave no similar bs issues. After I get my money&#x27;s worth many times over for thesei will likely invest in Wahl brand top end clippers for lifetime use.</li>

    <li> I have just finished my first cut with the Wahl Chrome Pro. I love it!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I do know something about hair grooming as I was at one time pursuing a career in hair styling for the film industry. Instead, I went into sound recording. But I still learned a lot about hair. The first thing you learn is that Wahl&#x27;s professional line of clippers in the top used brand of clippers by pros in the world. The second thing you learn is their reputation for quality and customer satisfaction.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So I felt pretty confident that I wanted a Wahl clipper set when I went looking for one. My hair cuts (basically a modified buzz cut) were costing me twenty dollars each by the stylist I was going to. She is good, and a pro, but sheesh, 20 bucks just to use a clipper to buzz off my hair? So having experience in the business, I looked around for prices at various places. The absolute best price was right here at Amazon. More on that in a minute.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So in opening up the kit (all of the many accessories are listed above) I removed the clipper from the kit, took the twisty tie off the cable, found the blade comb I wanted and immediately started clipping. No set up, no prep needed. I had washed my hair, let it dry, and combed it. To get the length I like, I already knew the comb numbers from past experience. Wahl, and all other hair experts recommend that you start with the comb that leaves the most hair on your head first. You can always work your way down quickly by using the next number comb (higher numbers leave more hair; the lower the number, the closer the cut).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;With my kind of cut, you do the sides and back first, around the ear next, and then finally the top. So I found a number four comb, clicked it onto the clipper, which is very easy, and then started in on one side of my hair. Using the Wahl clipper is so easy that with my kind of cut, I can do it all myself. A color booklet comes with the kit and is very easy to follow. Wahl also has DIY videos on YouTube to watch. You use the arch or rocking technique as you move the clipper up the side of the head, pulling the clipper away from the top as you finish your move. It is very easy and I was finished with both sides and the back in a couple of minutes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Next, I found the Right and Left taper combs to cut around the ear. You start at the lower edge of hair on each side and cut in a circle around the ear all the way to the front. The Chrome Pro has a taper lever on the side and this adds a greater degree of adjustment as you cut. It will lower and raise the cutting blades in case a comb isn&#x27;t quite low enough but the next comb would be too tight. Great feature!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After I was done with both ears, I put the number six comb on the clipper (they change out instantly) and starting at the front of my hair, cut straight back at first as the hair fell off. The clipper and combs cut evenly and professional looking. I finished the top of my head from the back, moving from all directions over the swirl to ensure an even cut. After that was done, I took off the combs and with the help of a mirror, used the clipper to trim the side angles of the back and a straight line across the bottom. Easy as anything. The last thing you do is use the barber shears and styling comb to even out any cow licks and clean up around the ears. To finish off, a wetting of the hair and some Bed Head gel and I&#x27;m ready for town!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After cleaning the clipper with the enclosed brush, it was back into the carry case and under the sink. I&#x27;ll use this every week and my hair will stay looking great without growing long and then getting cut short again. My wife, who was doing my hair more recently, absolutely loved the cut and said she&#x27;s retired fromcutting my hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have to mention price here.     <li> Pro: -The price -Some useful attachments -Durable storage case -Adjustable blade (zero gap can be done) -A T-Blade can be use to replace the blade -Cutting my hair a #3 all around and then getting a line-up/shape-up from my barber does save me some money. :)  Con: -It was loud, at first. To fix the problem TURN OFF the clipper and turn the power screw clockwise until it stops. Don&#x27;t force the plastic screw too much or else you may break the plastic screw. Then, turn it on and turn the plastic screw counter-clockwise until the noise is reduce. This definitely helped me. Now it sounds like a hair clipper from a barbershop.  By the way, the power screw moves the white plastic underneath the blade. Turning the power screw too much counter-clockwise can misaligned the blades. Check out this video for an idea. https://www.youtube.com/watch?v&#x3D;R7QdJ2QLpy4  Durability is questionable. I wouldn&#x27;t use this, if I were a barber.</li>
